Public Voice

Perish Together

— Yan Zheng

It's really getting more and more absurd. A ten-tael ingot of silver can be valued at more than seven thousand dollars. A US dollar can be exchanged for more than twenty national currency. Some people hoard rice and coal; others hoard cotton yarn and cloth. No matter what the commodity, it is sealed up and sent to the warehouse. It is said, "The price hasn't risen enough yet, not selling!"

Some also take out a little to sell, but their prices make you shake your head. The 工部局 (Gong Bu Ju) 's notice prohibiting the unauthorized raising of prices seems to have no effect at all.

They really want to squeeze every drop of the public's blood and sweat! Although they know very well that the public's purchasing power is dwindling. They are making "immediate money," squeezing as much as they can!

Some have already been squeezed naked and barefoot, even starving to death. Some have been squeezed almost dry, and have no choice but to shamelessly run back to their hometowns in the occupied areas. Those are the weaklings. But there are also those who are tough, unwilling to sit and wait, and take risks for "survival." Haven't you seen the social news reported in the past few days?

Regardless of whether the means are legitimate, "wanting to eat" is a common desire. By then, when they have lost the object of their wealth, it will be the time when they won't let you alone hold a golden bowl and eat leisurely!

At that time, even if you hoard gold bars and US dollars, you will perish together!

Save Everyone (Public Voice, Part 2)

— Someone

I am a small office worker in a foreign firm, with a monthly salary of fifty-six dollars. Before the war, it was not too shabby to support a family of three (wife and child). But the cost of living after the war has almost increased four or five times. Although I have requested a raise several times, the employer has only increased my salary by 15% and added a living allowance of ten dollars (totaling seventy-four dollars and forty cents). But to support this small family, even just dealing with food and housing is very pitiful.

Because a twelve-dollar attic before the war now costs eighteen dollars. Rice and food cost at least thirty dollars or more per month. Other things like coal briquettes, oil, salt, soy sauce, and vinegar are all frighteningly expensive. And what's worse is that in this round of price increases, "sitting and waiting for death" is certainly not an exaggeration.

Naturally, thinking a step back, someone like me with such an income could probably be classified as middle-class in this metropolis, right? In this wave of unemployment, I should be calm and patient, and endure this difficult time. But our current suffering is not directly affected by the war, which cannot be denied. People standing on the same boat not caring about the safety of the whole is what makes us have to stand up and shout loudly. At the same time, it is precisely because we are middle-class that it makes you wonder how those in the lowest class are supposed to survive?

There is a story that tells us:

When a great flood submerged a village, two brothers each carried all their belongings and fled in two small boats. On the way, the older brother felt that the younger brother's boat had more things than he did. The two argued, and the older brother secretly devised a plan to stun the younger brother, throw him into the water, and move the things from the younger brother's boat to his own. But that small boat was overloaded. When a wave hit, it sank, and the older brother naturally drowned in the water as well.

Chinese compatriots living on the "isolated island" are just like the brothers in that village. We should tie the two small boats together tightly to resist the current waves! Otherwise, the realization of this story is only a matter of time.

Save everyone! It is also saving yourself!

Recent Commodity Prices in Sichuan

— Hua Jian

I recently received a letter from a friend in Zigong, Sichuan, which included a summary of commodity prices in Sichuan. I am reprinting it below:

Rice: $10 per dou (peck) Blue calico: $1.40 per foot

Coal: 5-6 cents per catty (pound) White cotton cloth: $1.50-1.60 per foot

Pig lard: $1.20 per catty Washcloth: Over $2 per piece

Vegetable oil: $1.10 per catty Hemp yarn socks: $7-8 per pair

Chicken: Over $3 per bird Crepe satin: $3-4 per foot

Duck: Over $2 per bird Silk satin: $3-4 per foot

Fish: Over 10 cents per liang (ounce) Silk floss: $7-8 per catty

Meat: 65 cents per catty Cotton: 5-6 dollars per catty

Eggs: 5-6 cents per egg Gongni shoes: $12 per pair

White sugar: $1.40 per catty

Salt: 40 cents per catty

Tofu: 4 cents per block

From the above summary of commodity prices, we can see that commodity prices in Sichuan are not simply rising wildly. The prices of pig lard, vegetable oil, chicken, and duck are similar to those in Shanghai, as they are not entirely dependent on imported goods. The prices of eggs, meat, and salt are cheaper than in Shanghai because they are local products. However, blue calico, white bamboo cloth, hemp yarn socks, crepe satin, etc., are more expensive because they are entirely dependent on transportation from Shanghai or Hong Kong, which is quite different from the situation in Shanghai, where there is hoarding. However, blue calico, white bamboo cloth, hemp yarn socks, crepe satin, etc., are more expensive because they are entirely dependent on transportation from Shanghai or Hong Kong, which is quite different from the situation in Shanghai, where there is hoarding.

Poor Bones Can't Hold On Any Longer

— Jin Chuan

Public Voice, Part 3

Gold has risen and foreign exchange has shrunk, so the merchants are taking advantage of the situation again, licking blood from their knives. The burden of life has doubled, making it difficult for my few poor bones to support! I cry to heaven, but there is no response; I enter the earth, but there is no door. Rice costs fifty dollars, coal briquettes cost nine dollars. The prices of daily necessities are rising daily and are impossible to keep track of. They all open their mouths and raise prices by 30% or 50%. But our stomachs cannot go a day without food. However, life is so expensive that we cannot reach it. I do not have the magic of turning things into gold, and I am even considering whether pills can replace food. Even if the few poor bones are made of steel, steel will break; even if the blood is tap water, tap water will run dry. When we reach this point of broken bones and dried-up blood, the poor will all become starving corpses. The merchants' bellies will swell like graves, filled with so many poor bones. They can certainly make fortunes of hundreds of thousands of dollars, but it is likely that after a while, their bellies will burst and they will all perish together. Those on the sidelines will be happy and benefit. It chills me to think of it!

Confucius said, "Oppressive government is fiercer than a tiger!" Now, life is fiercer than a tiger! Tigers can be avoided, but the burden of life cannot be avoided!

Merchants, show some conscience and save hundreds of thousands of compatriots from becoming starving corpses. Otherwise, they will only die in front of you! But how long can you be happy?

After the Rain, the Sky Clears

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 23: Old Friends, New Companions, Writing is Valuable; Famous Scenic Spots, People in Charge Obtain

Therefore, in order to prevent the scenic spots from being defaced, the construction of private tombs in scenic areas is absolutely prohibited. Even in non-scenic areas, there are certain restrictions on the land occupied by tombs. Because the land is used for production, and after China's revival, we need to ensure that there are no wandering people in the countryside and no wasteland. However, so much land is occupied by the dead, which is too meaningless. Fortunately, there are now public cemeteries everywhere in China. A plot of public cemetery land can bury many people. Moreover, the practice of cremation is gradually becoming popular. Speaking of advertising, it is even more strictly prohibited in scenic areas. For example, in the past, whenever you encountered a place with the most beautiful scenery, with green mountains looming and blue waters stretching, you would want to relax on a pavilion and look into the distance. But there would always be a big billboard blocking your view, which would be very annoying. Not to mention advertisements for gonorrhea and eye diseases, with naked and ugly women painted on them, or warriors with upturned mustaches, which would make people feel uncomfortable. Even legitimate commercial advertisements are not allowed to be placed in scenic areas. Billboards are not prohibited, but if you want to attract attention, you can set them up in designated areas in the market. Why bother ruining the scenery? Not only are tombs and advertisements prohibited, but also private residences and villas are prohibited. Unless the building is open to the public and anyone can visit it, then it is considered public property. Although many pavilions and buildings have been built in the Yuantouzhu area, they are all public property. The place where Engineer Xue and his wife are entertaining guests is called Shuiyun Tower, which is a newly built building funded by the Taihu Cement Company and owned by the government. The scenery is very beautiful from the top of the building. After a while, Jin Danyun and his wife arrived with many people. Among them, many people had been to Yuantouzhu in Wuxi before, but Mrs. Su Liya and the two Miss He were visiting for the first time. Engineer Xue and his wife were very hospitable, and Jin Danyun and Mrs. Xue met for the first time and were even more cordial. The dishes they are serving today are called Chinese food eaten Western-style. What does it mean to eat Chinese food Western-style? It turns out that all the food materials are Chinese products, and the cooking method is also Chinese, but Western-style knives and forks are also prepared. They knew that Mrs. Su Liya was there today, and she was not used to Chinese chopsticks. But in fact, they did not know that Mrs. Su Liya had long been sinicized. She often eats with Chinese chopsticks, unlike Europeans and Americans who have just arrived in China and cannot handle chopsticks well. The dishes can be separated for each guest, but they are cooked together. The essence of Chinese cooking is to put everything together, like a country, which should be unified, not divided. (273)

Entertainment Industry

An Englishman's Bird's-Eye View of Hollywood

— Xin Liang

George Arliss, a well-known British star in Hollywood, recently published an article in the American "Modern Historical Materials" titled "Hollywood—In the Eyes of an Englishman." He described his life in the film industry for the past ten years and the conditions in Hollywood in great detail, vividly and interestingly. The following is a translated excerpt of the original text:

"Of all the cities I've lived in, Hollywood is the most comfortable. Most of the men and women walking on the streets are related to film companies. Even a star walking on the street won't be surrounded, although strangers may suddenly approach to ask their name and say hello.

"My first impression of Hollywood was that it was vast—everywhere you look, there are small villages. There aren't many tall shops and hotels...

"Except for the surrounding mountains, almost all the beauty of Hollywood is man-made.

"I once met a famous stage actor named Joseph Jefferson. I asked him what his interest in acting was like when he was young, and he told me: 'Acting was really hard back then; putting a piece of red cloth on a soapbox and forcing you to sit on it like an emperor, can you imagine how difficult that was?' But now, in Hollywood, all the costumes, sets, and props are so realistic that even if you don't want to be an emperor, you'll naturally feel majestic.

Secondly, George Arliss also told us about the hardships of many Hollywood actors, saying:

"In a film set, you don't necessarily need to know how to cook, how to be a good wife or a mother, but you must learn to be patient. If you're an extra, you have to be in the makeup room at the film set by 7:30 in the morning to prepare for your first shot. Then, you have to wait, wait, and maybe wait until late at night before filming starts. The next day, you have to go there early to wait again. Even a big star, though they can come a little later, can't avoid waiting. Often, after putting on makeup, they have to wait a long time before filming starts. During this time, you can't write letters, you can't read the newspaper, and that's really exhausting!"

Finally, he also told us: the so-called blockbuster hits are usually good films in reality, and definitely not crudely made imitations of others.

Arliss is also writing a book called "My Ten Years at the Studios" to permanently record his history in the film industry. It will soon be published by the American Littell and Brown Company.

Female Animal Tamer Chen Xiuying – Starred in the Film "Savage King" in Hong Kong

— Traveling Reporter

Wild beasts are fearsome, but to tame ferocious lions and tigers to be as docile as kittens and white rabbits can be seen in movies. Movies can often deceive and create illusions. However, in the circus, Miss Chen Xiuying's amazing skill of subduing tigers and taming elephants is performed live in front of millions of viewers.

Miss Chen is a Chinese overseas from Africa, 21 years old this year. She has been involved with the circus since she was a child. She has been performing for ten years since she was eleven. From Africa through East India to various parts of Southeast Asia, she and her seventy-odd companions in the troupe have wandered through hundreds of docks and more than a dozen countries in tents. Therefore, in addition to her animal taming skills, she can also speak seven different languages.

Four years ago, she learned the national language of her motherland very fluently and participated in many fundraisings for various just causes and good deeds for her motherland. She has had many opportunities to observe and study in circuses in Europe, especially taming lions and tigers, which are rarely seen among foreign women, let alone in China.

Her physique is quite healthy and her appearance is also very beautiful. According to her own words, she once filmed a Cantonese wild animal film "Savage King" for a film company in Hong Kong. Many film companies competed to sign long-term contracts with her, but the tent life of wandering has become too much of a love for her. Because she was reluctant to part with her companions of many years, she politely declined.

The African Circus came to Shanghai to perform this time. Due to acclimatization problems, they rested for a week during the opening. Now it is said that they will soon officially participate in the performance.

Affection of Two Leading Actors

Foreword to "The Wages of Sin"

— Qin

Who knew that Hedy Lamarr's seductiveness had an incredible magic. In the past blockbuster "Ecstasy", she had bold performances and erotic provocations that shocked movie fans around the world. "The Wages of Sin" is a representative work of her in Hollywood, and MGM has spared no effort to complete this masterpiece very solemnly.

In her recent works, the English she speaks cannot get rid of the vowels of her native language. But in "The Wages of Sin", she speaks fluent and pure English. This may be a miracle. She has only been in Hollywood for a short year, and she can speak so correctly. If it is not her special intelligence, how can she have such achievements? Not only that, but also in terms of expression and performance, she is exquisite and transparent. Whether it is facial lines, eye movements, or actions, she has very high achievements.

The entire plot undoubtedly touches everyone's heart, especially the sympathy of women. Hedy Lamarr is a woman who has been abandoned. She cannot withstand the oppression of material desires and carnal desires. She commits suicide. Fortunately, a doctor saved her life. In various encounters, she understands the greatness of true love. She abandons her social status and resolutely marries this doctor to do a work of compassion.

The male star who plays the doctor is Spencer Tracy, who starred in "Boys Town". This great artist who won the Academy Award for the Arts has a profound performance in the first time he performed love scenes, which shows his versatility and omnipotence.

The director is the famous Van Dyke, who has five years of stage experience and has been an assistant to the director giant Old Reifeis. Famous films such as "The Strange Case of Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde", "Eskimo", "Marie Antoinette", "The Thin Man", and "The Gun Beneath the Sea" were all directed by him and left a lofty reputation.

The above three artists have cooperated to create "The Wages of Sin". At least, it can be said that satisfactory appreciation is an inevitable fact. Anyway, it will be released at the Grand China today, and let the movie fans chew on it themselves!
